text:
I also thought muffins came out rather bland so I made a few alterations.  I would recommend substituting the white sugar with packed light brown sugar; increasing the spices to 1 1/4 tsp cinnamon, 3/4 tsp ground ginger, and 1/2 tsp nutmeg (I did not have any pumpkin spice or ground cloves); and increasing the pumpkin puree to 1 cup.  These changes produced more flavorful muffins.

text:
I made these and they were a big hit!! The people at the party I took them to claimed I had put an addictive substance in them :-)  

I used packed dark brown sugar instead of white, I used 1 cup of pumpkin instead of 3/4 cup, and I doubled the cinnamon and nutmeg.

I also made them into mini muffins, so I used mini chocolate chips.  cooking the minis for 15 minutes worked well.

text:
This was a great recipe although me and some of my taste testers thought there was too much chocolate chip.  I think I will try mini chocolate chips or chocolate shavings next time.  Also, I "wetted" the chips then put them in with the flour mixture before mixing in with the wet.  This coated them and helped to prevent the chocolate from falling to the bottom. These muffings are also wonderful with homemade cream cheese frosting!
oops one more thing, I found 400 was too high and burned the outside.  375 for 20 minutes was perfect.

text:
I doubled this recipe to make 2 dozen muffins.  I made the following changes to the recipe: applesauce in place of the oil, I used the entire can of pumpkin and the whole bag of chocolate chips.  I also just used PAM spray rather than liners or shortening + flour in the pans.  I followed the other reviews and only set the oven to 350.  They were done in 20 minutes and tasted fabulous!

text:
I love these muffins!  I make them two different ways: exactly as in the recipe (except maybe with a little more pumpkin) and with cream cheese.  Put half the normal amount of batter in each muffin cup, then add a dollop of cream cheese with a little bit of sugar added and finally put the rest of the batter on top.  Bake as the recipe states.  The muffins come out with a little surprise in the middle!

text:
This recipe is great!  I made about 4 batches yesterday varying the spices per the other reviews and found the best batch was with the following changes to the original recipe:  1 cup pumpkin (used fresh), omitted the salt & cloves (didn't have any), substituted brown sugar for white, 1 t. cinnamon, 1/2 t. nutmeg, 1/2 t. ground ginger and replaced the white flour with whole-wheat white.  I also found baking at 375-degrees for 20 minutes was perfect!  I gave these out as treats for my neighbors and everyone asked for the recipe...

text:
These are easy and come out good every time. I did make some changes to suit my family. But, even as is they are really good.  If the review says it's bland it's because the spices are old. Spices loose their flavor after a month or so on the shelf. My spices were fresh and doubling it was too spicey. This comes from an Indian family, so we eat lots of spicy curries and this was too much doubled. Perfect as is.  I added, 1/4 c sour cream, added 1/2 teaspoonn vanilla, and subbed milk for the water, increased pumpkin to 1 cup and baked at 350 (took 5-10 min longer). 375 at 20 minutes made them rise really well in a dark pan.  One cup of choc chips was plenty. Two was way too much. Even as wrote the easiest and best muffins I've made, this comes from a woman who has her own baking business! Thanks for sharing!

I always feel the need to tinker with a recipe so here goes: Increased pumpkin to 1 cup. Reduced the sugar to 1/2 cup, added 1/4 cup of buttermilk in place of water and then spices as follows:2 tsp. cinnamon, 1/2 tsp. ginger, 1/4 tsp cloves, eliminated allspice. Added 1/2 cup walnuts and 1/4 cup golden raisins.Didn't use the choc. chips as my husband wasn't home and he could'nt make me. He would put them in everything, a confirmed chocoholic:)Used paper muffin tin liners and preheated oven to 350 degrees and cooked the muffins for 18-20 minutes til my bakery poker came out clean. All the rest of the ingredients I used as in the recipe.House smelled spicey good.

text:
After reading the reviews, I think I'd like to say first that these are PUMPKIN MUFFINS.  If you're looking for a sweet roll, look elsewhere.  I made this exactly as is.  The pumpkin and spices are subtle, yes, I agree on that.  If the chocolate chips weren't in there, I probably would say they're too bland, but the chips, while being subtle also, give them just enough of an extra something to really "make" them.  They are easy, and moist.  I personally thought they were better after a day or two.  I gave some to two ladies at work who *loved* them.  Next time I may try applesauce instead of oil to cut some fat.  But then, not all fat is bad.

I am giving these a three as the recipe stands.  I spruced them up a bit and they still came out bland, so I can't imagine how bland the original recipe must be.  I used 1 c. pumpkin, doubled the spices, and a cup of chocolate chips.  They came out flavorful spice and chocolate wise, but they weren't sweet enough at all.  Next time, I would either take the brown sugar suggestions some people talked about or I would increase the white sugar to a cup.  The muffins are very moist and flavorful once you up the amount of spices, but it's missing the sweetness which would help to bring all of the flavors together.  I think I am going to make a powdered sugar glaze to put over the top of them to help add some sweetness to them.

text:
The first time I made this recipe I thought they were kind of bland, but in all fairness, I didn't have ground cloves, which would make a difference.  After reading the other reviews, I made these again as a double batch so in addition to doubling the ingredients, I used brown sugar instead of white, 2 cups of pumpkin, cinnamon applesauce in place of the oil and increased all the spices (including ground cloves this time) by at least 1/4 tsp (I didn't carefully measure my increases, I just added some) plus I added 1/4 tsp of pumpkin pie spice.  Wow!  This recipe started of good, but a little bland, but with the changes, the muffins are delicious!  Thanks to all who commented on changes in their reviews!  Update - I made these again yesterday using my changes above and using canned sweet potato casserole (Glory brand) because I couldn't find pumpkin and they were still delicious - you can't tell the difference....Yummy!

These are really yummy! A few suggestions, though:  instead of all flour, I added 3/4 cup flour and 3/4 cup Quaker oats to make healthier and heartier (the oats make the texture a bit more firmer, which we liked). text:
My extremely picky niece liked these!  I followed other reviewer's suggestions, and substituted applesauce for oil, upped the pumpkin (used one 16 oz can for a double batch), and lowered the oven temp to 350 and adjusted the baking time accordingly (used the toothpick test for doneness).  I also used mini milk chocolate chips-they seem to disperse better in the batter, instead of dropping to the bottom. They came out moist and yummy!  Remember that if you don't use any oil, the muffins will stick to cupcake liners, so you may want to spray the tins instead.  The recipe as written is fairly healthy (for a dessert), but eliminating the oil may tweak it just enough to make it truly a good-for-you snack (3 grams of fat per 100 calories)!  Definitely will make it again!

Will make again for sure!

text:
This combination is surprisingly tasty.  Go ahead and double the recipe, because they will disappear quickly!  

The muffins stuck to the paper wrappers, so I recommend spraying the pan instead.  I altered the recipe to make it even more healthy by using applesauce instead of the oil, using just one-half cup sugar, substiting whole wheat flour for one-third of the regular flour, and adding three tablespoons of gluten flour to help the muffins be fluffy.  I found that I liked the spices to be a little milder, so I used half as much nutmeg and cloves.  

These muffins are really easy to make, healthy, and delicious!

Some reviewers stated that they were bland.  I do not like muffins to be sweet; they are not supposed to be cupcakes. As others have said, this recipe is a bit bland and could stand a few substitutions but it's a keeper once you find out how you best like it!  It's definitely an EASY and fast recipe and makes the house smell wonderful!  As for substitutions, I, too recommend using brown sugar instead of white, applesauce instead of oil and perhaps some vanilla extract and more spices, more pumpkin.  This is actually great with a little cream cheese on top and  a cup of coffee on the side.  (By the way, I used mini choco chips and found that they were just big enough!)  Happy Baking!

text:
These are by far the best muffins I have ever made. Perfect texture and flavor.  Double the recipe to make two dozen...you can freeze them (but probably won't need to!). I used cinnamon burst chips instead of chocolate chip, because that's what I had on hand, but also because my husband doesn't love chocolate. Also, I used 2 cups of fresh pumpkin puree (for the double recipe) and did NOT use any extra water. They came out moist and dense...perfect!I added a dash of ginger and I also used 1 cup of white sugar and 1/2 cup light brown...I always feel a little brown sugar works well with these spicy kinds of recipes. Thanks for sharing...there were so many recipes on here and I am SO glad I chose this one!

These turned out PERFECT! So yummy!!!! So fluffy and moist!  Here are the changes I made: I used 1 cup brown sugar instead of the 3/4 white sugar. I used 1 cup pumpkin instead of 3/4 cup. I mixed the chocoloate chips in with the dry ingrediants (it helps all of the chips to not sink to the bottom). I added 1/4 tbs pumpkin pie seasoning. I liberally sprayed the tins with Pam, and they literally slid right out after they baked, nothing stuck! I also sprinkled a little ground cinnamon on top before I baked them, then I cooked it at 370* for 20 min and they are literally perfect! I topped each one off with a chocolate chip!

Ok, so here's what I did, after reading everyone's reviews: I used unsweetened applesauce in place of oil, which I definitely recommend. I used the whole can of pumpkin and all the spices as written, adding 1/4 tsp pumpkin pie spice. I "wet down" the chocolate chips before adding them, and I did *not* use paper liners. text:
Very good starter recipe! Here are the changes I ended up making to fit my taste:  1 cup sugar (instead of 3/4 cup)  1 cup fresh pumpkin puree (instead of 3/4 cup canned)  1 and 1/2 tsp water (fresh pumpkin naturally has a high water content)  1 tsp All Spice (and nothing else)  A touch more chocolate chips, but not quite 3/4 cup  Bake at 375 instead of 400 for 15 minutes    With those changes, they turned out perfect for me. The first batch I tried, I made with the recommended changes from Chibi Chef - bad move (for us anyway). talk about over powering spices! Mine and my husband's tongues were numb from the insane amounts of nutmeg and clove. I should have known better because nutmeg and clove are strong spices on    their own. So anyway, I do not recommend altering the spices to that extent. It's way too extreme and totally takes away from the pumpkin. You end up with Chocolate Chip Clove muffins! Anyway, this is a really good recipe. Maybe next time I'll try white chocolate chips or cranberries and walnuts - YUM!

These are pretty good, with a few modifications.  Based on several reviews, I used brown sugar instead of white, increased the pumpkin to 1 cup, and doubled the cinnamon and nutmeg.  I also dusted the chocolate chips with flour prior to mixing them in and they stayed distributed throughout the muffins very nicely. Overall a good recipe with just the tiniest bit of tweaking!

Pretty good!  I tripled the recipe.  I used 3/4c. white sugar and 1 1/2c. brown sugar, 1/4c. vegetable oil and 1/2c. applesauce, and a 29oz. can of pumpkin.  I didn't use any cloves.  I used 2t. of cinnamon, 1/2t. of nutmeg, and 1t. pumpkin pie spice.  I also added 2t. of vanilla.  I did not use chocolate chips, but next time I will try cinnamon chips.  I used a cookie dough scoop to fill the muffin cups.  I used 1 scoop for the mini muffins and 2 1/2 scoops for the regular.  I sprinkled the tops with cinnamon sugar.  The batch made 24 mini muffins (baked for 11 min.) and 24 regular muffins (baked for 20min).  We are still eating them warm with butter!  Very nice!

text:
I could not have found this recipe at a more perfect time!! While on a VERY late-night baking spree to make muffins for selling at the farmer's market the next morning, I was browsing for a normal chocloate chip muffin recipe to try. Instead, I found this, and the idea of using pumpkin seemed perfect. Earlier in the day, a can of pumpkin had rolled from my cabinet as I put away groceries... an omen? The weather had been unseasonably cool here in Tennessee (in the 70s instead of in the 90s as it usually is in August), and it feels just like October. The thought of offering pumpkin muffins in the cool of the morning during the farmer's market was very appealing. 

And eating one warm from the oven was wonderful... perfect, even. I actually spoke aloud to myself (at 1:30 am, mind you), "Wow, these are terrific." The only change that I made was adding more spices, because I love the smell and taste of a very nutmeggy, cinnamony, clovey pumpkin product. 

I sold several at the market, and they did seem to appeal to those who also felt the tinge of autumn. In fact, I sold more pumpkin chocolate chip muffins than I did of the other two flavors, blueberry and apple-cinnamon. And as I gave the remaining two to my mother ans sister afterward, I could see their tangible joy at taking a bite of fall in August. 

Thanks for the great recipe!

text:
My new favorite pumpkin recipe. Quicker to make than pumpkin bread!  Was a big hit!
Changes I think improved it:
- Upped it to 1 cup of pumpkin
- Didn't add the water 
- I sprinkle chocolate chips only on the top once batter is already in muffin tin. Makes a nice bite of chocolate followed by pumpkin flavor vs mixing chips into the batter. 
- Baked at lower temp. 375 F for 18 minutes comes out perfectly in my oven. Moist! I think 400 dries them out.

I made according to the recipe, using coconut oil as my vegetable oil (which I always do when baking).  These were a huge hit with my teenagers!  I only baked for 15 minutes and they were perfect.  They did stick to the muffin papers a bit, so when I made them again I sprayed the bottoms of my mufffin papers with oil. I might  try making with brown sugar next time as some of the other reviews suggested to see the difference.  Some reviewers thought these were bland, but I liked that they weren't too sweet or overpowering on the pumpkin.

Update: if you want fluffy muffins, substitute softened butter for the oil and cream it with the sugar. Also, if you're lazy like me, you can double the recipe and pour the batter into a loaf pan. Bake at 350F for about 45 min to an hour and you get a loaf with a beautiful crust on top. I had to cover mine with foil after 45 min because I didn't want the outside to get too hard.

text:
I wanted to love these muffins, but as written I think they are bland and dry. I made them twice. The first time I made them just as written. I had to take mine out of the oven 5 minutes early and they were still dry. My oven is calibrated perfectly; I check often. They didn't have any pop. The second time that I made them they were better, but I made these changes: subbed brown sugar for the white, added 1 T molasses, doubled the cinnamon, and I added 1/4 cup of applesauce to the recipe. The applesauce and molasses add moisture, but no additional fat. The molasses serves to develop the flavor a little more, and something about molasses  keeps things nice and moist. I lowered the oven temp to 375 and got 12 muffins out of the recipe. With those changes-- they are delectable!

Very easy to make and amenable to changes depending on your preference.  I made it with walnuts (2 handfuls), choco chips (again 2 handfuls), used egg beaters instead of real eggs, and a whole can of pumpkin (the normal size, not the gigantic ones).  I sprinkled them with powdered sugar when serving.  They aren't too sweet which is perfect.  The only thing I would change is decreasing the amount of nutmeg by 1/2 but that's just me.  My kids just loved them.  I think you could add some zucchini to this to hide more veggies for kids and would taste just as good.

I have used this recipe for YEARS. They are best if you let the flavors develop overnight, and if you use foil disposable baking cups, not the paper cups. Use EVOO.  I always bake 2 batches: the first one gets devoured on baking day - with a few left over for the next day.  The rest go into a ziplock bag and into the freezer for Black Friday.  Pop the ziplock bag straight into your car as you leave the house, and by the time Starbucks /fave coffee shop opens early  you can have your fave coffee or tea and a delicious homemade muffin to get you on to the next store.  :)

text:
I wanted to use up some of our dry ingredients, I decided to make these muffins (in the dead of summer). I thought they were pretty good -- I doubled the recipe to use up a whole 15 oz can of pumpkin. This is 1/4 cup more pumpkin than the recipe calls for, so I used half the oil. I didn't have cloves, so I added a bit more cinnamon. All other measurements were true to the recipe. I'd bake at 375 next time, as the outsides got just a little more done than I like. I highly recommend the extra pumpkin and spice, as others have suggested - I did it out of practicality, but the muffins are still just a little bit bland. 

Having worked in a bakery, I can say that muffins and cake breads really develop their flavor over a day. We baked pumpkin choco-chip muffins and they definitely tasted more "developed" after a day, so I'm sure that tomorrow morning, the muffins will have more flavor.

city:

country:

text:
Oh my GOD. These muffins are out of this world. The best muffins I've ever had, bar none. I love pumpkin (and chocolate!), but every pumpkin-themed baked good I've tried is just a little dry. But when I saw the great reviews for these I thought I'd give it a shot. I didn't change the recipe at all, save for the suggested 1 cup of chocolate chips, and erring on the side of a little extra pumpkin. I used muffin cups and baked them at 380 degrees for 20 minutes, because overdone=too dry! 

I was SHOCKED that I had made these when I took the first bite. They are incredibly moist, the pumpkin and spice are delicious but not overwhelming and the chocolate is...well, chocolate. I got countless compliments from my housemates and friends. 

One tiny note: I filled the baking cups just a little more than 2/3 full--maybe 3/4--and that gave me a really nice rounded top! It meant making 24 muffins with a doubled recipe--perfect.

These muffins turned out fantastic.  I read the reviews before making, and made some alterations to the recipe. Delicious!  I substituted applesauce for the oil and added about 2 tbls of ground flax.  I also substituted dark brown sugar for the white.  I used the entire can of pumpkin - what was I going to do with a little bit?  They turned out great!  I also used about 3/4 cup of chocolate chips and "wetted" them as another reviewer suggested and then coated them in the flour mixture so they didn't sink.  I also doubled the cinnamon and the nutmeg.  Before baking, I sprinkled them with raw sugar for a little crunch on top.  I baked them for 22 minutes at 375 and I live at ~5000 feet.  They are moist and delicious.  They are heavy from all of the pumpkin, but not dense.  Very nutritious!  I will make again and send the recipe to friends.

text:
Yummy!  I've been wanting to try these ever since sampling one at a Starbucks.  Of course I can't follow a recipe to save my life, so I made the following modifications based on what I had on hand: 1 c. whole wheat, 1/2 c. white flour; applesauce instead of oil, 1/2 cup sugar; doubled the cinnamon and nutmeg; omitted the cloves; added 1 t. ground ginger; added an extra big dollop of canned pumpkin; used 2 broken-up organic expresso dark chocolate bars, making chunks more than chips.  They made 6 jumbo muffins.  My only disappointment was they didn't taste "pumpkiny" enough.  So I'm thinking next time I'll use pumpkin pie puree or get the spice instead to add.
